            <a href="/wiki/Lindblum_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Lindblum (Final Fantasy XIII)">
             Lindblum
            </a>
           </i>
           , where their leader,
           <a href="/wiki/Cid_Raines" title="Cid Raines">
            Cid Raines
           </a>
           , asks Snow to help him find the other l'Cie so together they could free the people of Cocoon from the fal'Cie rule. While passing through the Gapra Whitewood, Lightning learns about Hope's mother and the boy's belief her death was Snow's fault. Hope reveals he followed Lightning to gain battle experience and become strong enough to face Snow and forms "Operation Nora," his plan for revenge. Although Lightning tries to convince Hope it was the Sanctum that killed his mother and not Snow, Hope vows to make both Snow and the Sanctum pay for her death. To dissuade Hope from his goal of revenge, Lightning suggests Hope talks with his father in Palumpolum.
          </p>
          <p>
           After making their way out of the Vile Peaks, Sazh and Vanille travel through the
           <a href="/wiki/Sunleth_Waterscape" title="Sunleth Waterscape">
            Sunleth Waterscape
           </a>
           towards
           <a href="/wiki/Nautilus_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Nautilus (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Nautilus
           </a>
           . Sazh confesses why he went to the Hanging Edge: his son, Dajh Katzroy, was made a Sanctum l'Cie by the fal'Cie
           <a href="/wiki/Kujata_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Kujata (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Kujata
           </a>
           during the incident at Euride Gorge, while Sazh and his son were there as tourists. Sazh suspected his Focus was to destroy Anima when Dajh sensed the Pulse Vestige in Bodhum and caused the Purge, having gained the ability to sense Pulsian beings. To save Dajh from becoming a Cie'th, a mindless shambling monster a l'Cie becomes if they fail their Focus, Sazh boarded the Purge train with Lightning to try and complete Dajh's Focus for him. Unbeknownst to Sazh, Vanille knows more about the Euride incident than she lets on.
          </p>
          <h3>
           <span class="mw-headline" id="Truths_Revealed">
            Truths Revealed
           </span>
           <span class="editsection">
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit Truths Revealed section">
             <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
             Edit
            </a>
           </span>
          </h3>
          <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093700/finalfantasy/images/2/28/Snow_Villiers.png">
            <img alt="Snow Villiers" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Snow_Villiers.png" data-image-name="Snow Villiers.png" data-src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093700/finalfantasy/images/thumb/2/28/Snow_Villiers.png/180px-Snow_Villiers.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Snow Villiers" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Snow_Villiers.png" data-image-name="Snow Villiers.png" height="101" src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093700/finalfantasy/images/thumb/2/28/Snow_Villiers.png/180px-Snow_Villiers.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Snow_Villiers.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Snow and Fang save Hope and Lightning.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           Arriving in Palumpolum, Hope leads Lightning underground to slip past the soldiers occupying the city. Lightning realizes she has been running away from reality by making the Sanctum her enemy and she now has Hope following suit. She tells him to end Operation Nora and talk with his dad. Returning to the surface, Lightning and Hope are surrounded by PSICOM troops. They are saved by Snow and Fang and the l'Cie are separated in the chaos with Lightning and Fang in one group and Snow and Hope in another.
          </p>
          <p>
           Fang is Vanille's companion and is looking to reunite with her, the true reason she is helping the Cavalry. Fang reveals she and Vanille are not only Pulse l'Cie but citizens of Gran Pulse, having received their Focus there long ago and entered crystal stasis, but they awoke in Cocoon within the Pulse Vestige several days ago, starting the chain of events that led Cocoon into chaos. Fang's l'Cie brand is different than the others', white and unchanging, meaning she doesn't have to worry about being turned into a Cie'th. However, as Vanille's brand is still active, Fang is adamant in wanting to complete their Focus whatever it may be to prevent Vanille from becoming a Cie'th. Fang apoligizes Lightning that she and Vanille were indirectly responsible for Serah becoming a l'Cie, and that someday she will awaken from crystal stasis. She explains how a l'Cie's brand advances to show how long they have until they become Cie'th.
          </p>
          <p>
           Elsewhere, Hope confronts Snow about his mother's death, intending on taking his revenge. His plans are foiled when a PSICOM warmech attacks them and Snow saves Hope from further harm by cushioning their fall from the rooftops. Snow apologizes to Hope for what happened to Nora and the two settle their differences. Fang, Lightning, Hope and Snow are reunited and head to the Estheim Residence where Snow recovers from his injuries while Hope informs
           <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_Estheim" title="Bartholomew Estheim">
            his father
           </a>
           of Nora's fate and repairs his relationship with him.
          </p>
          <p>
           While the party is busy formulating a plan to deal with the Sanctum, PSICOM officer
           <a href="/wiki/Yaag_Rosch" title="Yaag Rosch">
            Yaag Rosch
           </a>
           arrives with his troops. Snow tries to make them realize they wish to protect Cocoon and demands the Purge to be stopped, but Yaag claims the lives of Pulse l'Cie are not worth the risk of sparing, and that the Purge is demanded by the people of Cocoon. After a confrontation with an attack shuttle, Snow, Lightning, Hope and Fang are rescued by Rygdea and taken onboard the
           <i>
            Lindblum
           </i>
           with help from Cid.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141108155853/finalfantasy/images/6/6e/Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png">
            <img alt="Jihl taunts Sazh" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png" data-image-name="Jihl taunts Sazh.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141108155853/finalfantasy/images/thumb/6/6e/Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png/180px-Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Jihl taunts Sazh" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png" data-image-name="Jihl taunts Sazh.png" height="101" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141108155853/finalfantasy/images/thumb/6/6e/Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png/180px-Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Jihl_taunts_Sazh.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Jihl reveals the truth about Vanille to Sazh.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           Sazh and Vanille arrive at Nautilus where they watch a newsflash regarding the events in Palumpolum and the
           <a href="/wiki/Pompa_Sancta" title="Pompa Sancta">
            Pompa Sancta
           </a>
           parade, a dramatic re-enactment of the War of Transgression. Tired of running Sazh decides to turn himself for a chance of seeing his son one last time. Vanille protests and is about to reveal the truth about the Euride incident when
           <a href="/wiki/Jihl_Nabaat" title="Jihl Nabaat">
            Jihl Nabaat
           </a>
           , PSICOM's supreme commander, arrives with a PSICOM platoon and Dajh, who has been kept in PSICOM custody to discern his Focus. Upon reuniting with Sazh, Dajh turns to crystal and his Focus is revealed to be the capture of Pulse l'Cie. Jihl shows security footage from Euride Gorge and reveals the truth behind the incident: Dajh's transformation into a l'Cie was the result of Vanille and Fang's threat towards Kujata that had turned the nearest person, Dajh, into a l'Cie to protect itself.
          </p>
          <p>
           Furious, Sazh confronts Vanille, triggering the appearance of his Eidolon,
           <a href="/wiki/Brynhildr_(Summon)" title="Brynhildr (Summon)">
            Brynhildr
           </a>
           , which he brings under control with Vanille's help. In his grief, Sazh tries to shoot himself but is unable to do so, prompting the PSICOM soldiers to take him and Vanille into custody. They are taken aboard the
           <a href="/wiki/Palamecia_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Palamecia (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            <i>
             Palamecia
            </i>
           </a>
           to be transported to Eden for live execution. During their imprisonment Vanille reveals her origins to Sazh: she and Fang became l'Cie to fight Cocoon during the War of Transgression and entered crystal stasis on Pulse. Twelve days before the Purge they awoke in Cocoon, but Fang had lost her memory of their previous Focus. Not wanting any more people to get hurt because of them, Vanille lied to also have lost her memory and has been running from her fate ever since. Deeming themselves the enemies of Cocoon and their Focus thus to be linked to harming it, Fang had suggested the two of them attack Kujata in Euride Gorge to possibly recover their memories on their Focus. During the ruckus Dajh had been made l'Cie and Vanille and Fang had got separated, and they have been searching for each other ever since.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141110184248/finalfantasy/images/0/07/Garens_Daislir2.png">
            <img alt="Garens Daislir2" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Garens_Daislir2.png" data-image-name="Garens Daislir2.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141110184248/finalfantasy/images/thumb/0/07/Garens_Daislir2.png/180px-Garens_Daislir2.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Garens Daislir2" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Garens_Daislir2.png" data-image-name="Garens Daislir2.png" height="101" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141110184248/finalfantasy/images/thumb/0/07/Garens_Daislir2.png/180px-Garens_Daislir2.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Garens_Daislir2.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Galenth Dysley aboard the
             <i>
              Palamecia
             </i>
             .
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           Upon learning of Sazh and Vanille's incarceration, Lightning and the rest mount a rescue mission with help from Cid and the Cavalry. They board the
           <i>
            Palamecia
           </i>
           using a stolen PSICOM shuttle but their ruse is discovered. Sazh and Vanille escape their holding cell, recover their weapons, and fight their way through the ship. The l'Cie are reunited on a forward portion of the
           <i>
            Palamecia's
           </i>
           exterior, and, using one of PSICOM's militarized wyverns, head to the bridge. They face Galenth Dysley who kills Jihl and the entire bridge crew. Dismissing the l'Cie's assumption he is one of them, Dysley reveals he is the fal'Cie
           <a href="/wiki/Barthandelus" title="Barthandelus">
            Barthandelus
           </a>
           , the true master of Cocoon.
          </p>
          <p>
           After suffering defeat at the hands of the l'Cie, Barthandelus reveals the l'Cie's Focus is to become Ragnarok and destroy
           <a href="/wiki/Orphan" title="Orphan">
            Orphan
           </a>
           , the fal'Cie that powers all the other fal'Cie in Cocoon and holds it afloat over Pulse. Barthandelus claims Serah's Focus was to gather them together to be made l'Cie so they could bring about Cocoon's destruction, a revelation that cripples Snow. Barthandelus departs, leaving behind his familiar
           <a href="/wiki/Menrva" title="Menrva">
            Menrva
           </a>
           to serve as an airship for them to escape from the now-sinking battlecruiser. The l'Cie make their escape, avoiding pursuit from Yaag Rosch onboard
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/The_Proudclad" title="The Proudclad">
             The Proudclad
            </a>
           </i>
           , ending up inside the
           <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Ark" title="Fifth Ark">
            Fifth Ark
           </a>
           hidden underneath Eden. Fang and Vanille recall a legend concerning the purpose of the
           <a href="/wiki/Ark_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Ark (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Arks
           </a>
           , armories and training grounds for l'Cie.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141123221402/finalfantasy/images/7/7e/Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png">
            <img alt="Cid Raines Final Form" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png" data-image-name="Cid Raines Final Form.png" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141123221402/finalfantasy/images/thumb/7/7e/Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png/180px-Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Cid Raines Final Form" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png" data-image-name="Cid Raines Final Form.png" height="101" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141123221402/finalfantasy/images/thumb/7/7e/Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png/180px-Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Cid_Raines_Final_Form.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Cid reveals the truth in the Fifth Ark.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           The l'Cie's powers are fully awoken and deeper inside the Ark they come face-to-face with Cid Raines who reveals himself a Sanctum l'Cie and that every action of the l'Cie had been orchestrated by Barthandelus. He explains the fal'Cie desire Cocoon's destruction to summon the
           <a href="/wiki/Maker" title="Maker">
            Maker
           </a>
           , the creator of both fal'Cie and the world so the world would be reborn. Cid attacks the l'Cie to stop them from destroying Cocoon, but is defeated and turns to crystal despite defying his Focus, puzzling everyone.
          </p>
          <p>
           Shaken by the turn of events, the l'Cie reach a dead end. Snow decides to follow Cid's example and forget their Focus and fulfill Serah's final wish of saving Cocoon. While everyone else agrees, Fang turns on them, proclaiming that even though they might wish to save Cocoon she would rather follow their Focus to destroy it than see any of her friends become a Cie'th for defying it. Fang unwittingly summons
           <a href="/wiki/Bahamut#Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Bahamut">
            Bahamut
           </a>
           , and brings it under her control with the others' help, reluctantly agreeing to follow with their plan. The l'Cie discover a new path following Bahamut's "taming" and a Pulsian airship at the end, which they use to travel through a portal leading to Gran Pulse.
          </p>
          <h3>
           <span class="mw-headline" id="Terra_Incognita">
            Terra Incognita
           </span>
           <span class="editsection">
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit Terra Incognita section">
             <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
             Edit
            </a>
           </span>
          </h3>
          <p>
           The airship is attacked by a wild wyvern in the skies above Gran Pulse and the l'Cie become stranded in the valley of
           <a href="/wiki/Vallis_Media" title="Vallis Media">
            Vallis Media
           </a>
           . The party searches Gran Pulse for days looking for a way to remove their brands, but find no traces of human life. Sazh's
           <a href="/wiki/Chocobo_Chick" title="Chocobo Chick">
            Chocobo Chick
           </a>
           warns the party that Hope's l'Cie brand is advancing and he has fallen unconscious. They bring Hope back to the base camp and Vanille suggests they go to
           <a href="/wiki/Oerba" title="Oerba">
            Oerba
           </a>
           , her and Fang's hometown. Hope wakes up and tells them he should remain behind but his Eidolon
           <a href="/wiki/Alexander_(Summon)#Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Alexander (Summon)">
            Alexander
           </a>
           is summoned and brought under his control. After Hope is given newfound strength, the l'Cie come to believe the true purpose of the Eidolons is to give l'Cie hope instead of freeing them through death.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093033/finalfantasy/images/9/9f/Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png">
            <img alt="Fang Vanille Mah&#039;habara" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png" data-image-name="Fang Vanille Mah'habara.png" data-src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093033/finalfantasy/images/thumb/9/9f/Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png/180px-Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Fang Vanille Mah&#039;habara" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png" data-image-name="Fang Vanille Mah'habara.png" height="101" src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206093033/finalfantasy/images/thumb/9/9f/Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png/180px-Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Fang_Vanille_Mah%27habara.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Fang assures Vanille they now have a new family.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           Discovering a path to the
           <a href="/wiki/Archylte_Steppe" title="Archylte Steppe">
            Archylte Steppe
           </a>
           , the l'Cie begin their journey to Oerba. Along the way, Vanille claims she became Ragnarok during the War of Transgression and cracked Cocoon's shell as her previous Focus. While traversing the
           <a href="/wiki/Mah%27habara_Subterra" title="Mah'habara Subterra">
            Mah'habara Subterra
           </a>
           , Fang bluffs about remembering her past Focus to coax a confession out of Vanille. Fang claims she was the one who became Ragnarok and scarred Cocoon. Vanille tries to deny it but the shock from having her deepest lie exposed causes her Eidolon
           <a href="/wiki/Hecatoncheir_(Summon)" title="Hecatoncheir (Summon)">
            Hecatoncheir
           </a>
           to appear, confirming Fang's suspicions. Vanille and Fang defeat it, after which Vanille resolves to come to terms with her fate and stop running.
          </p>
          <p>
           The l'Cie traverse the remainder of the Mah'habara mines and use the fal'Cie
           <a href="/wiki/Atomos_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Atomos (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Atomos
           </a>
           to reach the
           <a href="/wiki/Sulyya_Springs" title="Sulyya Springs">
            Sulyya Springs
           </a>
           , where Vanille speculates Barthandelus lied to them about Serah's Focus, and that she had overcome her Focus and turned to crystal of her own will like Cid had. They reach
           <a href="/wiki/Taejin%27s_Tower" title="Taejin's Tower">
            Taejin's Tower
           </a>
           , a crumbling mechanical tower where the fal'Cie
           <a href="/wiki/Dahaka_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Dahaka (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Dahaka
           </a>
           makes its home. The
           <a href="/wiki/Menhirrim" title="Menhirrim">
            Menhirrim
           </a>
           there help them destroy the errant fal'Cie and reach the top of the tower from where the l'Cie ride a capsule down to the slopes of Oerba. They find the village covered in a blanket of snow-like crystal dust and infested with Cie'th. At the end of a crumbling railway overpass the l'Cie are shocked to find Serah waiting for them.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150201114554/finalfantasy/images/e/e4/Barthandelus_Second_Form.png">
            <img alt="Barthandelus Second Form" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Barthandelus_Second_Form.png" data-image-name="Barthandelus Second Form.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150201114554/finalfantasy/images/thumb/e/e4/Barthandelus_Second_Form.png/180px-Barthandelus_Second_Form.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Barthandelus Second Form" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Barthandelus_Second_Form.png" data-image-name="Barthandelus Second Form.png" height="101" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150201114554/finalfantasy/images/thumb/e/e4/Barthandelus_Second_Form.png/180px-Barthandelus_Second_Form.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Barthandelus_Second_Form.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Barthandelus confronts the l'Cie.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           Serah implores the l'Cie to become Ragnarok and destroy Orphan, but they refuse to believe her. She abandons the disguise and assumes Barthandelus's human form. The fal'Cie explains the reason Cocoon was created: the fal'Cie, desiring to summon the Maker, need a sacrifice large enough to attract the Maker's attention and that the deaths of Cocoon's inhabitants would cause a large enough disturbance in "the great beyond" for it to happen. The l'Cie engage Barthandelus in battle, determined to prevent this atrocity from being committed.
          </p>
          <p>
           After defeating him Barthandelus gloats how the citizens of Cocoon are fighting among themselves now that the resurrected Cid has become the new Primarch, angering the Cavalry for his supposed betrayal. He warns them the Cavalry is mounting an attack to destroy Orphan under the belief it would free Cocoon from the fal'Cie rule, and they have a choice: destroy Orphan themselves or let the people of Cocoon destroy it. He leaves behind another airship and returns to Cocoon to oversee the final stages of his plan. The l'Cie find an ancient record telling the War of Transgression's aftermath: the reason Fang hadn't destroyed Cocoon was because the goddess
           <a href="/wiki/Etro" title="Etro">
            Etro
           </a>
           intervened and turned her and Vanille to crystal before they could. Later, after Vanille and Fang's crystals were placed inside the Pulse Vestige, Barthandelus brought the Vestige into Cocoon so they could finish the job when they awoke. The party decides to return to Cocoon and either save Orphan or die trying. They board the airship and use a portal in Pulse's atmosphere to return to Cocoon.
          </p>
          <h3>
           <span class="mw-headline" id="Eden_Under_Siege.2FThe_Cradle_Will_Fall">
            <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Eden" title="Siege of Eden">
             Eden Under Siege
            </a>
            /The Cradle Will Fall
           </span>
           <span class="editsection">
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit Eden Under Siege/The Cradle Will Fall section">
             <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
             Edit
            </a>
           </span>
          </h3>
          <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150127210222/finalfantasy/images/6/62/Return_to_Eden.png">
            <img alt="Return to Eden" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Return_to_Eden.png" data-image-name="Return to Eden.png" data-src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150127210222/finalfantasy/images/thumb/6/62/Return_to_Eden.png/180px-Return_to_Eden.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Return to Eden" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Return_to_Eden.png" data-image-name="Return to Eden.png" height="101" src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150127210222/finalfantasy/images/thumb/6/62/Return_to_Eden.png/180px-Return_to_Eden.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Return_to_Eden.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             The l'Cie return to Cocoon.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           The l'Cie disrupt an ongoing race in Eden with their Eidolons, causing mass panic among the spectators and the deployment of a full PSICOM battalion along with the resident Guardian Corps unit. Barthandelus uses transgates to warp Pulse creatures and automata from both the surface of Gran Pulse and within the Fifth Ark into the city, causing mass hysteria. The l'Cie fight their way through soldiers and monsters alike while the Cavalry infiltrates the Primarch's office, where Cid, no longer under the thrall of Barthandelus, tells Rygdea his actions will lead Cocoon into ruin. At his request, Rygdea shoots Cid, ending his torment, and leads the Cavalry to confront Orphan at Edenhall, the seat of the Sanctum's power.
          </p>
          <p>
           The citizens take shelter at Edenhall and at the center of the complex, and the l'Cie spot crystal shards floating in the air. An illusion of Barthandelus appears telling them the shards are the
           <a href="/wiki/Soul_(Fabula_Nova_Crystallis)" title="Soul (Fabula Nova Crystallis)">
            souls
           </a>
           of the departed, and their presence signals the appearance of the
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Door_of_Souls" title="Door of Souls">
            Door of Souls
           </a>
           and the Maker's inevitable return, and tells them he has their "loved ones" captive. The Calvary soldiers and PSICOM troopers in their vicinity turn into
           <a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Sacrifice (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            Sacrifice
           </a>
           Cie'th, the result of Barthandelus branding them without giving them a Focus. They are confronted by Yaag Rosch, who, after being defeated for the second time, helps the l'Cie by ordering his soldiers to evacuate the city rather than search for the l'Cie and detonating
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/The_Proudclad" title="The Proudclad">
             the Proudclad
            </a>
            's
           </i>
           wreckage, sacrificing himself and ensuring the party won't be followed into
           <a href="/wiki/Orphan%27s_Cradle" title="Orphan's Cradle">
            Orphan's Cradle
           </a>
           , an alternate dimension serving as the true command center of Cocoon.
          </p>
          <p>
           Inside Orphan's Cradle the l'Cie discover the remainder of the Calvary soldiers have been converted into Cie'th. Guided by the fal'Cie Eden, they arrive at the Narthex, Orphan's resting place. Barthandelus destroys Serah's and Dajh's crystallized forms and commands the l'Cie to fulfill their destiny by destroying Orphan, thereby cutting the power fueling Cocoon's functions and causing it to crash onto the surface of the lowerworld. The l'Cie see through Barthandelus's illusions, and Barthandelus engages them in battle only to be defeated and sent sinking into a pool of liquid. Menrva, Dysley's familiar, dives into the pool allowing Barthandelus to rise up as the protective shell surrounding the dormant fal'Cie Orphan.
          </p>
          <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206094931/finalfantasy/images/a/a2/Orphan_1.png">
            <img alt="Orphan 1" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Orphan_1.png" data-image-name="Orphan 1.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206094931/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a2/Orphan_1.png/180px-Orphan_1.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="Orphan 1" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Orphan_1.png" data-image-name="Orphan 1.png" height="101" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150206094931/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a2/Orphan_1.png/180px-Orphan_1.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Orphan_1.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             The party faces the merged form of Barthandelus and Orphan.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           The l'Cie fight Orphan's first form, but fail to destroy him. Growing frustrated, Orphan reveals the reason fal'Cie make l'Cie: Each fal'Cie was created by the Maker for a defined purpose, and given finite power to accomplish the task, but humans have infinite potential to be anything they want to be through sheer willpower and determination. Thus fal'Cie make l'Cie to partake in the power inherent in humankind.
          </p>
          <p>
           Orphan tortures Vanille to force Fang to transform into Ragnarok. Seeing no way out of their situation, Fang submits but the others try to stop her. She overpowers them, causing everyone except her and Vanille to turn into Cie'th. Fang is attacked by the shambling remnants of her companions, triggering her transformation into an incomplete version of Ragnarok. Fang's Ragnarok is unable to destroy Orphan; only the outer shield dissipates before Fang reverts. Orphan revives Fang and tortures her to force her to transform into Ragnarok once more while a helpless Vanille watches her friend suffer. Meanwhile, Lightning, Snow, Sazh, and Hope relive the memories of their journey and find the strength of will to revert, though they believe their Cie'th forms were another fal'Cie illusion. As Vanille prepares to make a stand against Orphan, the others fire magic spells at Orphan and save Fang from the fal'Cie, who sinks into the pool.
          </p>
          <p>
           After giving themselves the Focus of saving Cocoon rather than destroying it, the party's l'Cie brands burn out and turn white. Orphan's true form rises from the pool, and reveals it shares the same desire as Barthandelus to summon the Maker, even if it means its death. As Orphan has shown its true colors as an enemy of Cocoon, and believing that if they can destroy Cocoon, they can also save it, the l'Cie destroy Orphan.
          </p>
          <h3>
           <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Dawn_of_a_New_Era">
            The Dawn of a New Era
           </span>
           <span class="editsection">
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit The Dawn of a New Era section">
             <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
             Edit
            </a>
           </span>
          </h3>
          <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
           <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20130228033227/finalfantasy/images/a/a4/CrystalizedCocoon.png">
            <img alt="CrystalizedCocoon" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="CrystalizedCocoon.png" data-image-name="CrystalizedCocoon.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20130228033227/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a4/CrystalizedCocoon.png/180px-CrystalizedCocoon.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
            <noscript>
             <img alt="CrystalizedCocoon" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="CrystalizedCocoon.png" data-image-name="CrystalizedCocoon.png" height="101" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20130228033227/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a4/CrystalizedCocoon.png/180px-CrystalizedCocoon.png" width="180"/>
            </noscript>
           </a>
           <figcaption>
            <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:CrystalizedCocoon.png">
            </a>
            <p class="caption">
             Cocoon, crystallized by Ragnarok.
            </p>
           </figcaption>
          </figure>
          <p>
           With Orphan's demise the rest of Cocoon's fal'Cie shut down as the now-powerless structure descends towards Gran Pulse. Finding themselves back in Eden, Lightning and the others float away and begin to crystallize while Fang and Vanille join hands to summon Ragnarok's true form. Ragnarok creates a column of lava, which engulfs the surface of Cocoon and slows its descent. Ragnarok crystallizes the lava by summoning the crystal dust from the ruins of Oerba, leaving Cocoon supported by a massive
           <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Pillar_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Crystal Pillar (Final Fantasy XIII)">
            crystal pillar
           </a>
           entrenched on Pulse's surface. Their Focus fulfilled, Lightning, Hope, Sazh and Snow are crystallized on the surface of Gran Pulse.
          </p>
          <p>
           Through an unknown force, Lightning and her companions wake up from their crystal sleep. Finding their l'Cie brands gone, the group is reunited with Serah and Dajh who were also revived and are normal humans again. While the Cocoon survivors rally around the remaining military units as they see Gran Pulse for the first time, Hope takes a moment to mourn for Fang and Vanille while Lightning gives Serah her blessing to marry Snow. Within the core of the crystal pillar holding Cocoon above Gran Pulse, the crystallized forms of Vanille and Fang float, still holding hands, their Focus complete.
           <br style="clear:both"/>
          </p>
          <div class="notice metadata spoiler footer" style="border-top: 2px solid #dddddd; border-bottom:2px solid #dddddd; padding: 0.2em; overflow:auto;">
           <i>
            <b>
             <span class="endspoiler">
              Spoilers end here
             </span>
             .
            </b>
           </i>
          </div>
         </div>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
           Music
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit Music section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20091105033237/finalfantasy/images/d/d7/FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg">
           <img alt="FFXIII LE OST" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII LE OST.jpg" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20091105033237/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d7/FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg/180px-FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg" height="150" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII LE OST" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII LE OST.jpg" height="150" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20091105033237/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d7/FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg/180px-FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII_LE_OST.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            The soundtrack's limited edition.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <i>
            Main article:
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII:_Original_Soundtrack" title="Final Fantasy XIII: Original Soundtrack">
             Final Fantasy XIII: Original Soundtrack
            </a>
           </i>
          </dd>
         </dl>
         <p>
          <a href="/wiki/Masashi_Hamauzu" title="Masashi Hamauzu">
           Masashi Hamauzu
          </a>
          , one of the composers of
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_X:_Original_Soundtrack" title="Final Fantasy X: Original Soundtrack">
            Final Fantasy X: Original Soundtrack
           </a>
          </i>
          and the composer of the
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Dirge_of_Cerberus_-Final_Fantasy_VII-_Original_Soundtrack" title="Dirge of Cerberus -Final Fantasy VII- Original Soundtrack">
            Dirge of Cerberus -Final Fantasy VII- Original Soundtrack
           </a>
          </i>
          , composed the music for
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          . The game's vocal theme is called "
          <a href="/wiki/Kimi_ga_Iru_Kara" title="Kimi ga Iru Kara">
           Kimi ga Iru Kara
          </a>
          " ("Because You're Here"), performed by the J-pop artist
          <a href="/wiki/Sayuri_Sugawara" title="Sayuri Sugawara">
           Sayuri Sugawara
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Nobuo_Uematsu" title="Nobuo Uematsu">
           Nobuo Uematsu
          </a>
          was originally announced as the composer of the game's vocal theme, but later decided to give the duties to Hamauzu after being hired to work on
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIV" title="Final Fantasy XIV">
            Final Fantasy XIV
           </a>
          </i>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
           <a href="#cite_note-3">
            [4]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          The Japanese soundtrack was released on January 27, 2010 with two versions available for purchase. The standard version contains four discs while the limited edition contains a bonus "
          <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_Episode_Zero_-Promise-#Drama_CD" title="Final Fantasy XIII Episode Zero -Promise-">
           drama CD
          </a>
          " written by scenario writer
          <a href="/wiki/Motomu_Toriyama" title="Motomu Toriyama">
           Motomu Toriyama
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          In the game's western versions
          <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">
           Leona Lewis
          </a>
          sings the English theme song, titled "
          <a href="/wiki/My_Hands" title="My Hands">
           My Hands
          </a>
          ".
          <a href="/wiki/Yoshinori_Kitase" title="Yoshinori Kitase">
           Yoshinori Kitase
          </a>
          explained the decision to use a different song was made due to difficulties translating the lyrics of "Kimi ga Iru Kara" into English, and thus "My Hands" was chosen as the lyrics of the song still fit the game's theme.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
           <a href="#cite_note-4">
            [5]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In the game's western versions the song "Eternal Love" was replaced with "
          <a href="/wiki/FINAL_FANTASY_XIII_-_The_Promise#.22Serah.27s_Theme.22_Lyrics" title="FINAL FANTASY XIII - The Promise">
           Serah's Theme
          </a>
          ".
         </p>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">
           Development
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit Development section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020182758/finalfantasy/images/a/a3/FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg">
           <img alt="FFXIII PS2 version2" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII PS2 version2.jpg" data-src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020182758/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a3/FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg/180px-FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg" height="126" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII PS2 version2" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII PS2 version2.jpg" height="126" src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020182758/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a3/FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg/180px-FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII_PS2_version2.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Snow and Nora in the Hanging Edge in a PS2 beta version.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          In
          <i>
           Famitsu
          </i>
          , Kitase revealed the initial project concept for
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was thought of in 2004 when the
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X-2 International
          </i>
          team came up with the idea during a jogging session.
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was originally planned as a
          <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">
           PlayStation 2
          </a>
          game, but the development was moved to PlayStation 3 following May 2005
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
           <a href="#cite_note-5">
            [6]
           </a>
          </sup>
          and the team had to restart making the game assets from scratch. The development of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          happened during a time when Square Enix were shifting to a new console generation, and to a certain extent had to anticipate what the future generation would be like. The game was originally developed under the working title "COLORS WORLD".
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
           <a href="#cite_note-6">
            [7]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          only had development on the PlayStation 2 at the very beginning of the project, mainly focused around creating the world and story. The team working on
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was derailed when they were commissioned to create the
          <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_VII_Technical_Demo" title="Final Fantasy VII Technical Demo">
           <i>
            Final Fantasy VII
           </i>
           technical demo
          </a>
          for PlayStation 3; the demo's results were so promising the development of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was moved to this platform as well.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
           <a href="#cite_note-7">
            [8]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The idea from the start was to have a highly action-based battle system.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anniversary_8-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Anniversary-8">
            [9]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          The development was led by Yoshinori Kitase and as such, the development team resembles that of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X-2
          </i>
          , although occasionally, developers from
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XV" title="Final Fantasy XV">
            Final Fantasy XV
           </a>
          </i>
          (then known as
          <i>
           Final Fantasy Versus XIII
          </i>
          ) assisted with the game's development.
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was developed on the Crystal Tools engine since the production moved on PlayStation 3. The process of making the company's first PlayStation 3 title proved to be a challenge as the team found it a tricky console to code for.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anniversary_8-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Anniversary-8">
            [9]
           </a>
          </sup>
          Determined to crack the puzzle, Square opted to create its own development kit, which became known as Crystal Tools.
         </p>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100121183548/finalfantasy/images/a/ac/FFXIII_fire.jpg">
           <img alt="FFXIII fire" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII_fire.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII fire.jpg" data-src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100121183548/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/ac/FFXIII_fire.jpg/180px-FFXIII_fire.jpg" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII fire" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII_fire.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII fire.jpg" height="101" src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100121183548/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/ac/FFXIII_fire.jpg/180px-FFXIII_fire.jpg" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII_fire.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Reveal trailer with a mock up battle menu with battles taking place on the field map.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          The overarching concept of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was "a future world fantasy" and "people fighting against fate."
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
           <a href="#cite_note-9">
            [10]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The concept for the battle system was to maintain the strategic nature of command-based battles, but to create battles similar to those seen in the film
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_VII:_Advent_Children" title="Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children">
            Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children
           </a>
          </i>
          . According to art director
          <a href="/wiki/Isamu_Kamikokuryo" title="Isamu Kamikokuryo">
           Isamu Kamikokuryo
          </a>
          , many additional areas that were functioning in an unreleased build, from team NORA's secret base, to Lightning's home and even a zoo, were cut from the game owing to concerns about the game's length and volume. Kamikokuryo additionally remarked that the volume of cut content was enough to make another game. Later, hackers have unveiled the dummied location
          <a href="/wiki/Seventh_Ark" title="Seventh Ark">
           Seventh Ark
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was first revealed at E3 2006. Since then, the battle system was changed several times. In the
          <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_E3_2006_Trailer" title="Final Fantasy XIII E3 2006 Trailer">
           first trailer
          </a>
          the camera angles and shifts were more dynamic and Lightning had a gravity-controlling ability that influenced the gameplay, lending to a somewhat more action-based and cinematic presentation than the final, more classic battle system. In the
          <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_Demo" title="Final Fantasy XIII Demo">
           playable demo
          </a>
          , the battle transitions were nearly seamless as the exploration and battle fields were very similar in appearance, unlike in the final game where the differences between the two fields are much more apparent.
         </p>
         <p>
          It was revealed at E3 2008 that
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          would be released on the Xbox 360 and the PlayStation 3 in North America and Europe, but would remain a PlayStation 3 exclusive in Japan. A demo version of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was released with
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_VII:_Advent_Children_Complete" title="Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children Complete">
            Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children Complete
           </a>
          </i>
          in Japan on April 16 exclusively for PlayStation 3. Covering a part from the early stages of the game, the demo aimed to familiarize players with the battle system, while featuring Cocoon and the l'Cie. Only Lightning and Snow were playable, with Sazh, Lebreau and Gadot supporting them during battles. The demo was not released outside of Japan.
         </p>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020175639/finalfantasy/images/c/c7/FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png">
           <img alt="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" data-image-name="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020175639/finalfantasy/images/thumb/c/c7/FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png/180px-FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" data-image-name="FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" height="101" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20141020175639/finalfantasy/images/thumb/c/c7/FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png/180px-FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII-Prerelease-Battle.png">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Early battle HUD.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          "Re: Final Fantasy XIII" is a promotional DVD that was released by Square Enix in Japan on December 13th, 2008, to advertise the upcoming games of the
          <i>
           Fabula Nova Crystallis: Final Fantasy
          </i>
          series. Said to be included were never-before-seen trailers, along with the rarely seen trailers shown at the DKS3137 conventional event. The DVD is reported to be fifty minutes and includes the first look at real
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          gameplay. Included on the DVD as well were promos for
          <i>
           Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children Complete
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Dissidia_Final_Fantasy" title="Dissidia Final Fantasy">
            Dissidia Final Fantasy
           </a>
          </i>
          , and movies for non-
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          Square titles. A second demo was featured in the
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          Premiere Party and Tokyo Game Show in September 2009, showcasing the summons as well as the Paradigm Shift system. Again, only Lightning and Snow could be controlled in battle, while Sazh, Vanille, and Hope were supporting party members.
         </p>
         <p>
          The initial screenshots of the Xbox 360 version Square Enix released to compare to the PlayStation 3 version were revealed, in fact, to be screenshots from the PlayStation 3 version, with the Xbox 360 icons pasted on top. Square Enix apologized, claiming it was a mistake, and later released genuine Xbox 360 screenshots. The Xbox 360 version runs at 576p (FMV CG 576p), as opposed to the PlayStation 3's native resolution of 720p (FMV CG 1080p), but both versions can be upscaled to 1080p.
         </p>
         <p>
          Similar to
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XI
          </i>
          , and
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XII
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          has only English and Japanese audio with subtitles localized to local languages.
         </p>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="A_Problematic_Development">
           A Problematic Development
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit A Problematic Development section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <p>
          After the game's release, Square Enix has revealed that
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII'
          </i>
          s development was a difficult one and ridden with miscommunication between different sections of the development team.
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          had the largest development team of any previous
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          game, with some of the work also done in conjunction with the
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XV
          </i>
          team (then-titled
          <i>
           Final Fantasy Versus XIII
          </i>
          ). At the peak, there were over 200 people working on it, with 180 artists, 30 programmers, and 36 game designers.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gama_10-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Gama-10">
            [11]
           </a>
          </sup>
          According to the October 2010 issue of
          <i>
           Game Developer
          </i>
          magazine
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Game.252520Set.252520Watch_11-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Game.252520Set.252520Watch-11">
            [12]
           </a>
          </sup>
          , a big problem during the game's development was the lack of unified vision. The game was first announced at 2006, but the E3 trailer was merely a visual concept and the team hadn't created anything playable yet, leading to pressure within the development team on what the battle system should be like. What further complicated the development was that the team was also working on Square Enix's multi-platform engine Crystal Tools. The team made the mistake of trying to accommodate every single project in progress and a considerable amount of time was spent prioritizing all the different requests and the team was not able to determine the final spec requirements. It created a standstill between the engine and game development teams; if the engine's specs couldn't be finalized, neither could the game's.
         </p>
         <p>
          Being a large-scale project Square Enix wanted to keep details of the game secret, but this led to the international player testing being too late, which further led to scheduling constraints as the team wanted to ensure the game would appeal to Western audiences. The development team was well-aware of criticism toward JRPGs coming from North America and Europe concerning game linearity and command-based battles; the development team experimented with Western development methods and international focus groups were set up for certain titles, including
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          However, at this time the development team was already far along in development and it was too late to implement most of the feedback. Despite this, the team was able to gain some insight into what players wanted globally, but also led to conflicts because the development team didn't receive clear instructions on whether to force certain changes into an already tight schedule. Much of the feedback which was unable to be included in
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          , was later used when developing
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII-2
          </i>
          .
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gama_10-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Gama-10">
            [11]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20101016223721/finalfantasy/images/a/a3/Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg">
           <img alt="Ff13snowbattle demo" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg" data-image-name="Ff13snowbattle demo.jpg" data-src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20101016223721/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a3/Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg/180px-Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg" height="97" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Ff13snowbattle demo" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg" data-image-name="Ff13snowbattle demo.jpg" height="97" src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20101016223721/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a3/Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg/180px-Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:Ff13snowbattle_demo.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            Demo gameplay.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          The game's overall vision did not fully realize until the demo included with
          <i>
           Final Fantasy VII: Advent Children Complete
          </i>
          , because even at a late stage of development, the team did not agree on the game's key elements. The team had to make adjustments to the schedule to accommodate the demo, but after it was complete, the team finally had a tangible version of the game that could actually be played, which unified the vision and understanding of the game's direction across the entire development team. Before the demo, different elements for the game had been created with no clear plan on how they would be used in the final game. With the demo pulling all the strings together, the team could prioritize to help increase productivity.
         </p>
         <p>
          The way the development team has come out open with the problems with
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII'
          </i>
          s development is rather unique, and may reflect the polarized reception the game received after its release.
          <br style="clear:both"/>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Localization">
           Localization
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit Localization section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was being localized for English as it was being made, but it had no infrastructure to support simultaneous development and localization. There were no content freeze deadlines to ensure the translators were translating with the final context, and cut scenes were still changing after the English voice recording was finished. The entire voice script ended up being re-recorded about four or five times. The translators would have to translate blindly from text, and then see an early render to notice it would not work. When placeholder audio would show up the translators would realize their lines wouldn't match the timing or the emotion that would be on the characters' faces. The translators had scripts from the writers, videos of events, transcripts of the actual Japanese voice data, and the latest game build, but all four would be different and none of them final.
         </p>
         <p>
          Tom Slattery, who was handling the English localization, and Teruaki Sugawara, the sound engineer, who also subsequently left the company, were both serving as representatives from their respective departments at the monthly meetings between Sound and Localization, and both realized that if that was going to be the way localization was handled on subsequent projects, there needed to be a way of keeping all information synchronized without placing unnecessary burden on the development team, Sound, or Localization. When
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII-2
          </i>
          would be developed, the developers would use a tool called Moomle to do just that.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGamer_12-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-RPGamer-12">
            [13]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          Jack Fletcher did voice directing and casting for
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          ; his previous experience in the series includes
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy X-2
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XII
          </i>
          , and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_Tactics" title="Final Fantasy Tactics">
            Final Fantasy Tactics
           </a>
          </i>
          . Around twenty auditions were held for the important characters and Square Enix would let Fletcher cast the rest on his own by giving him character descriptions on how they wanted the characters to sound.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Union_13-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Union-13">
            [14]
           </a>
          </sup>
          For lead and cameo characters the producers would want to hear at least five to eight different voice samples per character to choose from.
         </p>
         <p>
          The voice directing team would then pick portions from the game script to send to agencies and get auditions back from them. It has also been mentioned that Square Enix does not want to reuse voice actors too much, so anyone who has played a lead role before is unlikely to get another
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          lead part soon, and so, even if
          <a href="/wiki/Ashelia_B%27nargin_Dalmasca" title="Ashelia B'nargin Dalmasca">
           Ashe's
          </a>
          voice actress Kari Wahlgren submitted a good audition, Square would not want to cast her as Lightning.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Union_13-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-Union-13">
            [14]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The idea to cast two characters with Australian accents came from the localization team, who requested the voice directing team to look for either Australian or New Zealand sounding voices; the rationale was that the team wanted Fang and Vanille to sound like they were from another world, but more in a sense of having a different melody to their voices, rather than a thick accent.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Union_13-2">
           <a href="#cite_note-Union-13">
            [14]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Employee_Departures">
           Employee Departures
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit Employee Departures section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <p>
          The problematic development of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          led to the departure of several members of the development team, who left Square Enix during development or on the game's release, including:
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toshiro_Tsuchida" title="Toshiro Tsuchida">
            Toshiro Tsuchida
           </a>
           (battle planning director)
          </li>
          <li>
           Takashi Ohkuma (background technical director)
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Masashi_Hamauzu" title="Masashi Hamauzu">
            Masashi Hamauzu
           </a>
           (composer), who went freelance
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Nao_Ikeda" title="Nao Ikeda">
            Nao Ikeda
           </a>
           (sub-character designer), who went freelance
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
            <a href="#cite_note-14">
             [15]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
         </ul>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">
           Themes
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit Themes section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <div class="spoilers collapsible" data-rel="themes">
          <div class="header" style="border-top:solid 2px #ddd; border-bottom:solid 2px #ddd; overflow:auto;">
           <b>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_Wiki:Spoiler_Policy" title="Final Fantasy Wiki:Spoiler Policy">
             <span style="color:red">
              Spoiler warning
             </span>
            </a>
            :
            <i>
             Plot and/or ending details follow.
            </i>
           </b>
           <i>
            (
            <span class="skiplink">
             <a href="#.23">
              Skip section
             </a>
            </span>
            )
           </i>
          </div>
          <p>
           The main themes of
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           are challenging fate and the concept of willpower. The main cast has an unjust fate (Focus) forced upon them and seek a way to escape it and do what they believe is right. Ultimately free will triumphs over fate, as the party rejects their Focus and follows their true desire, to save Cocoon. The themes are present with the characters of Serah and Cid Raines, who similarly defy their fate, and with the interactions of Hope and his father, who tells Hope he must find his own path in life. The fal'Cie are on the other side of this coin, unable to follow their heart's desire as their fate is predetermined by their creator.
          </p>
          <p>
           Despite lacking magical powers and immortality like the fal'Cie, humans are still implied to be stronger in the end due to possessing free will, and Orphan explains to the party that humans' infinite potential is why fal'Cie chose to make l'Cie of men to carry out tasks they themselves are unable to do. Having a white l'Cie brand may represent a human's free will triumphing over the bond of a fal'Cie-given Focus, as in the end of the game, all of the party's l'Cie brands burn out, which is known to halt the process of turning into a Cie'th.
          </p>
          <p>
           Many characters in
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           suffer great losses in losing their homelands and loved ones, and the different ways they deal with their losses are at the center of their character arcs. While their first reaction is anger and vengeance, the party must come to terms with their losses and ultimately realize that revenge is futile, and the only way to cope is to move forward. Related themes are the themes of guilt and running away from the past, the things the party are forced to face if they wish to move on.
          </p>
          <p>
           Other central themes in
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           are theocracy, a system of government that rules under a single God recognized as the supreme ruler, and totalitarianism, a government system in which all aspects of life are controlled by the supreme ruler and any opposition is forbidden. Following theocracy, the Sanctum of Cocoon is ruled by the fal'Cie Eden that communicates through Primarch Dysley, who acts as Eden's messenger and makes its orders known to the rest of Cocoon. In accordance to totalitarianism, the military forces follow the Sanctum's policies without question and ensure the populace follows suit, justifying their actions by claiming them to be for the greater good of everyone and necessary to keep the peace, and willing to go as far as fire upon unarmed civilians who try to escape or resist.
          </p>
          <p>
           The Sanctum uses propaganda and false pretenses to control the public and cover up its true intentions, the prime example being the Purge, a method to slaughter civilians supposedly tainted by Pulse by pretending to cast them out to the lowerworld, "execution masquerading as exile" as Lightning points out. The Cocoon society pushes their own fears away by Purging anyone connected to Pulse, and it is a personal revelation to Lightning when she realizes she is doing the same in having initially set out to destroy Eden.
          </p>
          <p>
           Another theme is the union of two worlds. For centuries, the people of Gran Pulse and Cocoon have despised and lived in fear of each other. Those from Cocoon are conditioned by the fal'Cie acting through the Sanctum to believe Gran Pulse to be hell and to fear and hate anything having to do with Pulse. The people of Pulse call Cocoon a "floating nest of vipers" and hate the people of Cocoon for luring Pulsians to their world and stealing their resources. The party realize their two worlds and their people are more similar than they thought. It is when Gran Pulse and Cocoon are connected by the crystal pillar formed by Ragnarok that the hostility ends and the two worlds become one.
          </p>
          <div class="notice metadata spoiler footer" style="border-top: 2px solid #dddddd; border-bottom:2px solid #dddddd; padding: 0.2em; overflow:auto;">
           <i>
            <b>
             <span class="endspoiler">
              Spoilers end here
             </span>
             .
            </b>
           </i>
          </div>
         </div>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Release">
           Release
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit Release section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <div class="floatright">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100729143844/finalfantasy/images/a/a0/Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" title="Special Edition PS3 with Lightning on the console.">
           <img alt="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive" class="lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" data-image-name="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" data-src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100729143844/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a0/Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg/300px-Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" height="189" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="300"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive" class="" data-image-key="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" data-image-name="Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" height="189" src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100729143844/finalfantasy/images/thumb/a/a0/Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg/300px-Final-fantasy-xiii-ps3-slim-japan-exclusive.jpg" width="300"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was released on December 17th, 2009 in Japan exclusively for PlayStation 3. Coinciding with the release a Japanese alcoholic beverage distributor Suntory released the energy drink
          <a href="/wiki/Elixir_(Energy_Drink)" title="Elixir (Energy Drink)">
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           Elixir
          </a>
          to promote the game's release. A PlayStation 3 bundle called "Lightning Edition," which includes a copy of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          , was released in Japan on the same day. 200 units were allocated to be sold in Taiwan. It contains a Ceramic White PlayStation 3 slim 250GB set with pink Lightning artwork.
         </p>
         <p>
          On November 13th, 2009 the game creators released a video with interviews and new footage that announced the game's international release date. One month prior to the game's release, Square Enix had begun promoting the game via a tour bus where gamers could preview and play the game, until March 9th, 2010,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          was released worldwide on both PlayStation 3 and Xbox 360.
         </p>
         <figure class="article-thumb tleft show-info-icon" style="width: 150px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100730123225/finalfantasy/images/9/99/FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png">
           <img alt="FFXIII Collector Edition" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png" data-image-name="FFXIII Collector Edition.png" data-src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100730123225/finalfantasy/images/thumb/9/99/FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png/150px-FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png" height="170" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="150"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII Collector Edition" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png" data-image-name="FFXIII Collector Edition.png" height="170" src="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100730123225/finalfantasy/images/thumb/9/99/FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png/150px-FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png" width="150"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII_Collector_Edition.png">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            The entire contents of the Limited Collector's Edition.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          A Limited Collector's Edition of the game was released exclusively in PAL territories. It contains the game packaged with the following exclusive content:
