         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           Artwork of all six party members with their respective Eidolons.
          </li>
          <li>
           Two stickers of the Pulse l'Cie brand.
          </li>
          <li>
           The Original Sound Selection, which includes composer Masashi Hamauzu's comments on the ten tracks comprising the selection.
          </li>
          <li>
           A hardback book, titled
           <i>
            The World of Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           , which contains scenario information for the game.
          </li>
         </ul>
         <p>
          A special Xbox 360 bundle was available for the North American, European, Australian, and New Zealand releases of the game. The bundle included a 250GB Xbox 360, 2 wireless controllers and a copy of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          is the first game in the series to receive an official release in Chinese. The localization uses the original Japanese audio with traditional Chinese subtitles, and was made by SEC Asia. Unofficial translations call
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          "Space Warrior" (), but
          <a href="/wiki/Yoshinori_Kitase" title="Yoshinori Kitase">
           Yoshinori Kitase
          </a>
          kept the name "Final Fantasy" for consistency.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
           <a href="#cite_note-15">
            [16]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          The game was released as an Ultimate Hits International Edition on Xbox 360 in Japan on December 16, 2010. It includes a brand new
          <a href="/wiki/Difficulty_Level" title="Difficulty Level">
           Easy Mode
          </a>
          and is packaged with the following content:
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           An artwork booklet, titled
           <i>
            FINAL FANTASY XIII -Corridor of Memory-
           </i>
           with visual art from both Japan and overseas.
          </li>
          <li>
           <i>
            FINAL FANTASY XIII
           </i>
           Unused Event Scenes, a look at scenes cut from the game with an accompanying script.
          </li>
          <li>
           An epilogue novel, titled
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_-Episode_i-" title="Final Fantasy XIII -Episode i-">
             Final Fantasy XIII -Episode i-
            </a>
           </i>
           , which reveals the events after the end of the game.
          </li>
         </ul>
         <p>
          The International release also includes "My Hands" as its theme song instead of "Kimi ga Iru Kara".
         </p>
         <p>
          On July 21st, 2011, the Japanese PlayStation 3 version of the game, got a free update, which introduced Easy Mode difficulty, to get on par with the Japanese Xbox360 version released a year earlier.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
           <a href="#cite_note-16">
            [17]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The update also disables the use of
          <a href="/wiki/Attack_Formations#Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Attack Formations">
           preemptive attack
          </a>
          to the
          <a href="/wiki/Ochu_(Final_Fantasy_XIII)" title="Ochu (Final Fantasy XIII)">
           Ochu
          </a>
          enemies, and disables the
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20090519091509/finalfantasy/images/6/64/Playstation-Button-R1.png" title="R1">
           <img alt="Playstation-Button-R1" class="lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="Playstation-Button-R1.png" data-image-name="Playstation-Button-R1.png" data-src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20090519091509/finalfantasy/images/6/64/Playstation-Button-R1.png" height="24" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="24"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="Playstation-Button-R1" class="" data-image-key="Playstation-Button-R1.png" data-image-name="Playstation-Button-R1.png" height="24" src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20090519091509/finalfantasy/images/6/64/Playstation-Button-R1.png" width="24"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          menu when walking to access the Shroud menu.
         </p>
         <p>
          The official Japanese website revealed a web novelization titled
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_Episode_Zero_-Promise-" title="Final Fantasy XIII Episode Zero -Promise-">
            Final Fantasy XIII Episode Zero -Promise-
           </a>
          </i>
          that contains a series of short stories written by
          <a class="new" href="/wiki/Jun_Eishima?action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jun Eishima (page does not exist)">
           Jun Eishima
          </a>
          leading up to the game events. The first story is called "Encounter," and focuses on Serah becoming a Pulse l'Cie. The second story is called "Stranger," and is about the moment Vanille and Fang awoke from crystal stasis, and began adjusting to Cocoon life. The third story, "Family," focuses on Sazh and his son, Dajh, detailing how Sazh came to own the Chocobo Chick and how Dajh fell into the Sanctum's clutches.
         </p>
         <p>
          The fourth story, "Search," details Vanille and Fang's separation, Fang's encounter with Cid Raines, and joining him to locate Vanille. Part five of the novel is titled "Friends," and focuses on Hope Estheim's life with his family and friends before his mother's death. The sixth story, titled "Present," involves Snow buying
          <a href="/wiki/Engagement_Necklace" title="Engagement Necklace">
           engagement necklaces
          </a>
          and Serah finding a
          <a href="/wiki/Birthday" title="Birthday">
           birthday
          </a>
          present for Lightning. The seventh and final story, called "Tomorrow," is about Fang and Vanille preparing to become l'Cie during the War of Transgression, and Vanille getting ready to be Purged to Gran Pulse.
         </p>
         <p>
          A multi-chaptered novella titled
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_Side_Story:_A_Dreaming_Cocoon_Falls_into_the_Dawn" title="Final Fantasy XIII Side Story: A Dreaming Cocoon Falls into the Dawn">
            Final Fantasy XIII Side Story: A Dreaming Cocoon Falls into the Dawn
           </a>
          </i>
          included in the
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII_Ultimania_Omega" title="Final Fantasy XIII Ultimania Omega">
            Final Fantasy XIII Ultimania Omega
           </a>
          </i>
          tells the stories of individuals in Cocoon that occur during the Purge and the Pulse l'Cie's journey.
         </p>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Release">
           Post-Release
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit Post-Release section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Sales">
           Sales
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit Sales section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <p>
          In Japan
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          sold over a million units on its first day of sale and had sold over 1,600,000 copies in Japan at the end of 2009.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
           <a href="#cite_note-17">
            [18]
           </a>
          </sup>
          In March 2010, Square Enix stated that
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          is the fastest selling title in the series' history. By April American game sales reached an estimated 800,000 units for PlayStation 3 and 500,000 units for Xbox 360. As of June 9th, 2011,
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          has sold over 6.5 million copies worldwide.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
           <a href="#cite_note-18">
            [19]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
           Reception
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit Reception section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 200px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100722033214/finalfantasy/images/d/d9/FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg">
           <img alt="FFXIII-Crystarium" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100722033214/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d9/FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg/200px-FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" height="113" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="200"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII-Crystarium" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" height="113" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100722033214/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d9/FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg/200px-FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg" width="200"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII-Crystarium.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            The Crystarium System was one of the game features that fell under criticism due to emphasizing the game's linear nature.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          received favorable reviews in Japanese game media and was voted as the second best game of 2009 in Dengeki Online's reader poll, and in January 2010, was voted "the best game ever" in
          <i>
           Famitsu'
          </i>
          s reader poll. The game's
          <a class="external text exitstitial" href="http://www.metacritic.com/games/platforms/ps3/finalfantasy13" rel="nofollow">
           Metacritic
          </a>
          score stands at 83 for the PlayStation 3 and 82 for the Xbox 360, signifying "generally favorable" reviews. However, this score is the lowest of all the offline main series
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          titles after the Nintendo DS re-release of
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_III" title="Final Fantasy III">
            Final Fantasy III
           </a>
          </i>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          has been hailed as a technical milestone with the presentation of CGI cutscenes and the almost seamless transition of visual quality between them and real-time gameplay. Many have appreciated the game's soundtrack though some feel the replacement of the game's original theme song with Leona Lewis's "My Hands" was unfortunate. The game's battle system has been generally liked, with the increased battle speed and the depth of the Paradigm Shift system. The story, characters and voice acting were mostly received well with reviewers stating the characters worked well together, and the interactions among them made up for shortcomings in the storyline.
         </p>
         <p>
          Many, however, reacted negatively to the game's linear nature especially in the first ten chapters on Cocoon compounded by the absence of traditional
          <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">
           towns
          </a>
          and little interaction with
          <a href="/wiki/Non-Player_Character" title="Non-Player Character">
           non-player characters
          </a>
          . Many also noted that the slow pace the game opens up, with the Crystarium System only expanding at certain storyline points to allow the characters to learn more abilities, and the rather late point in the game the player is allowed to choose their battle party, contributed to the game's linear feeling, some citing it "boring".
         </p>
         <p>
          The game director Motomu Toriyama has since stated the lower-than-expected review scores were a result of reviewers approaching the game with a Western point-of-view, and that reviewers were used to games in which the player was given an open world to explore; he noted this expectation contrasted with the development team's vision in that it "becomes very difficult to tell a compelling story when you're given that much freedom".
         </p>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          ended up being unexpectedly polarizing and is the first
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          main title to get such a strong reaction from the fans, that even Square Enix CEO, Yoichi Wada, acknowledges it, saying in a Gamasutra interview that "... when it comes to the customers' reaction to the quality of the game, some value it highly and some are not very happy with it".
         </p>
         <p>
          When the game was rereleased in October 2014 for PC, the game received a "mixed reception" and at its lowest favor rate from the players had 41% of positive reception. Among many issues that made the players disappointed were locked 1280720 resolution, lack of graphic settings, stuttering, and lag. The game later receives "mostly positives" user reviews on Steam after Square Enix releases a patch update to fix most of the issues in December 2014.
         </p>
         <h4>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">
           Controversies
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit Controversies section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h4>
         <ul>
          <li>
           Initial screenshots of the Xbox 360 version released by Square Enix to compare to the PlayStation 3 version were revealed shortly after to be screenshots from the PlayStation 3 version, with the Xbox 360 control icons pasted on top. Square Enix apologized, claiming there would be no need to enhance the Xbox 360 screenshots and that a mistake was made, and later released screenshots that did come from the Xbox 360 version. Though the screenshots were of low quality, including one with a mouse pointer over it, analysis of the new screenshots and later technical analysis by DigitalFoundry of both versions of the game revealed that the Xbox 360 version runs at 576p (FMV CG 576p), as opposed to the PlayStation 3's native resolution of 720p (FMV CG 1080p). Both versions can be upscaled to 1080p.
          </li>
          <li>
           On June 2nd, 2010, a class action lawsuit was filed against Square Enix and Sony Computer Entertainment America due to alleged freezing bugs in the game damaging and physically breaking PlayStation 3 consoles. Square Enix claims it is an issue with the console, while Sony blames the issue on a glitch on the game disc.
          </li>
          <li>
           In August 2010, a television advert of
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           was banned in Britain by the Advertising Standards Authority due to Square Enix advertising the Xbox 360 version of the game with footage of the PlayStation 3 version exclusively.
          </li>
          <li>
           After the confirmation that an Xbox 360 port of
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           would be released in Japan, CEO Yoichi Wada received death threats from angry fans accusing him of being a liar.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
            <a href="#cite_note-19">
             [20]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
         </ul>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels">
           Sequels
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit Sequels section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <p>
          A sequel titled
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII-2" title="Final Fantasy XIII-2">
            Final Fantasy XIII-2
           </a>
          </i>
          was announced on January 18th, 2011.
         </p>
         <p>
          Square Enix registered a domain name for
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII-3
          </i>
          on September 7th, 2011, but no development plans were announced. A representative of Square Enix noted that the filing is to protect the
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          intellectual property and is not indicative of a new title. On September 1st, 2012,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Lightning_Returns:_Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Lightning Returns: Final Fantasy XIII">
            Lightning Returns: Final Fantasy XIII
           </a>
          </i>
          was announced, which is said to be the last installment in the story of Lightning.
         </p>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">
           Ports
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit Ports section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Microsoft_Windows_and_Steam">
           <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">
            Microsoft Windows
           </a>
           and
           <a href="/wiki/Steam" title="Steam">
            Steam
           </a>
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit Microsoft Windows and Steam section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <div class="floatright">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20140919235826/finalfantasy/images/d/d5/FFXIII_Steam2.jpg" title="Logo for Steam Store.">
           <img alt="FFXIII Steam2" class="lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII_Steam2.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII Steam2.jpg" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20140919235826/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d5/FFXIII_Steam2.jpg/250px-FFXIII_Steam2.jpg" height="117" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="250"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII Steam2" class="" data-image-key="FFXIII_Steam2.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII Steam2.jpg" height="117" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20140919235826/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/d5/FFXIII_Steam2.jpg/250px-FFXIII_Steam2.jpg" width="250"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
         </div>
         <p>
          Square Enix announced at Tokyo Game Show 2014 that
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII-2" title="Final Fantasy XIII-2">
            Final Fantasy XIII-2
           </a>
          </i>
          , and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Lightning_Returns:_Final_Fantasy_XIII" title="Lightning Returns: Final Fantasy XIII">
            Lightning Returns: Final Fantasy XIII
           </a>
          </i>
          are coming to PC and Steam.
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          arrived first on October 9, 2014. The game features English and Japanese dubs, and subtitle in English, French, Italian, German, and Spanish.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
           <a href="#cite_note-20">
            [21]
           </a>
          </sup>
          The Japanese and Asian version have Japanese audio only, with subtitle in English, Traditional Chinese, and Korean.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
           <a href="#cite_note-21">
            [22]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          The game runs capped at 60FPS. Both Xinput and DirectInput controllers are supported.
         </p>
         <p>
          A patch update will be released in December 2014. Customizable rendering resolution options are included.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
           <a href="#cite_note-22">
            [23]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>

         <h4>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Steam_Trading_Cards">
           Steam Trading Cards
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit Steam Trading Cards section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h4>
         <p>
          The Steam version of
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          comes with 6
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steam_Trading_Cards" title="Steam Trading Cards">
           Steam Trading Cards
          </a>
          ; all of them feature Lightning.
         </p>

         <h3>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="iOS_and_Android">
           iOS and Android
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit iOS and Android section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h3>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright show-info-icon" style="width: 180px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150410160850/finalfantasy/images/d/da/FFXIII-iOS.jpg">
           <img alt="FFXIII-iOS" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="FFXIII-iOS.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII-iOS.jpg" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150410160850/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/da/FFXIII-iOS.jpg/180px-FFXIII-iOS.jpg" height="101" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="180"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="FFXIII-iOS" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="FFXIII-iOS.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII-iOS.jpg" height="101" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20150410160850/finalfantasy/images/thumb/d/da/FFXIII-iOS.jpg/180px-FFXIII-iOS.jpg" width="180"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <a class="sprite info-icon" href="/wiki/File:FFXIII-iOS.jpg">
           </a>
           <p class="caption">
            <i>
             Final Fantasy XIII
            </i>
            on mobile devices.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          became playable on
          <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">
           iOS
          </a>
          and
          <a href="/wiki/Android_(System)" title="Android (System)">
           Android
          </a>
          systems April 10th 2015 via the App Store and Google Play in Japan. The game, distributed by Broadmedia Corporation, runs on smartphones thanks to G-cluster Global Cloud Technology, meaning players need to be connected to the internet to play. The application is free to download and try for the first 30 minutes, with a 2,000 yen in-app purchase allowing users full access.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
           <a href="#cite_note-23">
            [24]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <p>
          The game being played on a server and the footage is sent to the player's device that in return sends controller inputs back over the air. Square Enix recommends players play on a wi-fi network with a stable 3Mbps connection.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
           <a href="#cite_note-24">
            [25]
           </a>
          </sup>
          <br style="clear:both"/>
         </p>

         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Packaging_Artwork">
           Packaging Artwork
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit Packaging Artwork section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          is the first
          <i>
           Final Fantasy
          </i>
          title with European packaging artwork that does not only feature the game's logo, but the main protagonist as well.
         </p>
         <div class="proto-gallery FFXIIIa" style="border-radius:1em;clear:both;">

               <img alt="FFXIII Amano" class="" data-image-key="FFXIII_Amano.jpg" data-image-name="FFXIII Amano.jpg" height="150" src="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20120806210432/finalfantasy/images/thumb/8/8a/FFXIII_Amano.jpg/114px-FFXIII_Amano.jpg" width="114"/>

         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Allusions">
           Allusions
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit Allusions section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <dl>
          <dd>
           <i>
            Main article:
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII/Allusions" title="Final Fantasy XIII/Allusions">
             Final Fantasy XIII/Allusions
            </a>
           </i>
          </dd>
         </dl>
         <p>
          <i>
           Final Fantasy XIII
          </i>
          contains numerous allusions to the number thirteen, as well as references to various world mythologies, among others.
         </p>
         <h2>
          <span class="mw-headline" id="Trivia">
           Trivia
          </span>
          <span class="editsection">
           <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIII?action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit Trivia section">
            <img class="sprite edit-pencil" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D"/>
            Edit
           </a>
          </span>
         </h2>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright " style="width: 60px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img3.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329230127/finalfantasy/images/8/81/XboxChocobo.png">
           <img alt="XboxChocobo" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="XboxChocobo.png" data-image-name="XboxChocobo.png" data-src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329230127/finalfantasy/images/thumb/8/81/XboxChocobo.png/60px-XboxChocobo.png" height="62" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="60"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="XboxChocobo" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="XboxChocobo.png" data-image-name="XboxChocobo.png" height="62" src="http://img4.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329230127/finalfantasy/images/thumb/8/81/XboxChocobo.png/60px-XboxChocobo.png" width="60"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <p class="caption">
            Chocobo for X360 Avatar.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <figure class="article-thumb tright " style="width: 60px">
          <a class="image image-thumbnail" href="http://img1.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329225623/finalfantasy/images/2/2a/PSICOMuniform.png">
           <img alt="PSICOMuniform" class="thumbimage lzy lzyPlcHld " data-image-key="PSICOMuniform.png" data-image-name="PSICOMuniform.png" data-src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329225623/finalfantasy/images/thumb/2/2a/PSICOMuniform.png/60px-PSICOMuniform.png" height="208" onload="if(typeof ImgLzy==='object'){ImgLzy.load(this)}" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D" width="60"/>
           <noscript>
            <img alt="PSICOMuniform" class="thumbimage " data-image-key="PSICOMuniform.png" data-image-name="PSICOMuniform.png" height="208" src="http://img2.wikia.nocookie.net/__cb20100329225623/finalfantasy/images/thumb/2/2a/PSICOMuniform.png/60px-PSICOMuniform.png" width="60"/>
           </noscript>
          </a>
          <figcaption>
           <p class="caption">
            Male PSICOM Uniform for X360 Avatar.
           </p>
          </figcaption>
         </figure>
         <ul>
          <li>
           During the development, models of
           <a href="/wiki/Yuna" title="Yuna">
            Yuna
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Rikku" title="Rikku">
            Rikku
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Ashelia_B%27nargin_Dalmasca" title="Ashelia B'nargin Dalmasca">
            Ashe
           </a>
           , and
           <a href="/wiki/Vaan" title="Vaan">
            Vaan
           </a>
           were used as stand-ins for characters that weren't finished yet.
          </li>
          <li>
           The PlayStation 3 version came with a code that, when registered with Square Enix's community website, allowed one to register to be a beta tester for
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XIV" title="Final Fantasy XIV">
             Final Fantasy XIV
            </a>
           </i>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           In the lead-up to the release of
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           , Microsoft ran a promotion where a Chocobo Avatar item would become available if a certain amount of the hashtag '
           <a class="external text exitstitial" href="http://twitter.com/#search?q=%23FFXIIIXBOX" rel="nofollow">
            #FFXIIIXBOX
           </a>
           ' had been used on Twitter or if one registered with an email. The chocobo looks and behaves similarly to the one Sazh carries around with him.
          </li>
          <li>
           Players who registered a first production run of the Xbox 360 version at the
           <a class="external text exitstitial" href="http://member.square-enix.com/na/" rel="nofollow">
            Square Enix Members
           </a>
           site received download codes for Male and Female PSICOM uniforms for their Xbox Live Avatar.
          </li>
          <li>
           The game was originally planned to have
           <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_Content" title="Downloadable Content">
            downloadable content
           </a>
           (DLC) released after the game, but Square Enix scrapped the plans.
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
            <a href="#cite_note-25">
             [26]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </li>
          <li>
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           is the first main series game to not feature either the original "
           <a href="/wiki/Prelude" title="Prelude">
            Prelude
           </a>
           " or "
           <a href="/wiki/Victory_Fanfare" title="Victory Fanfare">
            Victory Fanfare
           </a>
           ".
          </li>
          <li>
           <i>
            Final Fantasy XIII
           </i>
           marks the fourth time Square Enix has enlisted a non-Asian vocalist (Leona Lewis) to perform a vocal piece for a
           <i>
            Final Fantasy
           </i>
           soundtrack, after
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_X" title="Final Fantasy X">
             Final Fantasy X
            </a>
           </i>
           ,
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_X-2" title="Final Fantasy X-2">
             Final Fantasy X-2
            </a>
           </i>
           , and
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Dissidia_Final_Fantasy" title="Dissidia Final Fantasy">
             Dissidia Final Fantasy
            </a>
           </i>
           .
          </li>
          <li>
           An Easter Egg exists where if the player spins the analog stick as is common for grinding in previous games, the player character will stop and get irritated.
          </li>
          <li>
           The game was released in Japan on December 17, 2009, a day before the anniversary of the original
           <i>
            <a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy" title="Final Fantasy">
             Final Fantasy
            </a>
           </i>
           which was released in Japan on December 18, 1987.
          </li>
         </ul>
